Local News

Yesterday's Third Preparatory Meeting of Beijing-Guangdong Representatives 135

The So-Called Uniformity in Foreign Affairs Received Clear Explanation Yesterday

The Central Political System Will Be Further Discussed Today

Both Sides' Representatives Yesterday Telegraphed Guangdong to Express Condolences for the Death of Gu

The Beijing and Guangdong representatives held the third preparatory meeting at the same location yesterday morning at 10:00 AM. Guangdong representative Zou Lu was absent due to illness, and Beijing representative Li Shizeng also requested Wu Tiecheng to represent him due to illness. The meeting continued to discuss foreign affairs issues and the reform of the central system. The first item on the meeting agenda was concluded yesterday, and the discussion of the fifth item began, but no concrete results were achieved. The meeting adjourned at 12:00 PM, and it was decided to continue the discussion at the fourth preparatory meeting today. The proceedings of yesterday are summarized below:

He and Wang Met Before the Meeting　Wang Jingwei arrived at the meeting at 9:00 AM. While he was meeting with Wu Chaoshu, He Yingqin came to the meeting to visit Wang due to some important matters. Wang then met with He in another room. Subsequently, Chen Youren, Sun Ke, Fu Bingchang, Li Wenfan, and Nanjing representatives Chen Mingshu, Zhang Jingjiang, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Ji, and Wu Tiecheng arrived one after another at 9:30 AM. Li Shizeng was absent due to illness and was still represented by Wu Tiecheng. Zou Lu was also absent due to a cold. At 9:55 AM, He finished talking with Wang, and then announced the opening of the meeting at about 10:00 AM. The two sides discussed for about two hours and adjourned at 12:00 PM.

Situation During the Meeting　The General Assembly issued a statement yesterday regarding the situation of the meeting, stating that at today's (i.e., yesterday's) meeting, Chairman Cai Yuanpei read the Prime Minister's will. Representative Wang gave a temporary report, stating that he had just received a telegram from Guangdong comrades informing him that Mr. Gu Xiangqin had passed away at 6:00 PM yesterday (i.e., the day before), and proposed a three-minute silence to express condolences. All representatives stood in silence and performed the ceremony. First, more detailed and thorough discussions were held on the foreign affairs issue, and a decision was made on further measures (the publishable content is recorded separately below). Then, the discussion on the improvement of the central political system was continued. After the representatives expressed their opinions as much as possible, it was decided to summarize the various opinions into a proposal, which will be further discussed at the fourth meeting tomorrow (i.e., today).

Yesterday's Discussion of the Fifth Item　According to inquiries by this newspaper's reporter, at yesterday's meeting, Guangdong representative Wu Chaoshu first raised the so-called issue of limited uniformity in foreign affairs. After discussion among the participants, the following decision was made. As a result, the first item in the seven principles proposed in the letter from the Guangdong representatives, namely, "First seek uniform action in foreign affairs," was concluded. The second and third items did not need to be discussed. The fourth item concerned party affairs. The original text of the fifth item was "The Chairman of the National Government is proposed to be modeled after the presidential systems of France and Germany, with a senior and respected comrade serving as the chairman, and active military personnel should not be elected." Following the order, the fourth item should not have been discussed. Because the fifth item was more urgent, Sun Ke proposed to start the discussion. There were many opinions from the representatives, and it was decided to continue the discussion today.

Minutes of the Three Meetings　The General Assembly officially issued the agenda yesterday as follows: (A) Attending representatives: Chen Mingshu, Zhang Ji, Chen Youren, Sun Ke, Wang Zhaoming, Li Wenfan, Wu Chaoshu, Zhang Jingjiang, Cai Yuanpei, Wu Tiecheng, chaired by Cai Yuanpei, with Cheng Zhonghang, Yang Zongjiong, Qiu Jinxian, and Zhong Tianxin as recorders. (B) Resolutions: (1) The following explanation was made regarding uniformity in foreign affairs: The so-called uniformity in foreign affairs is limited, such as non-resistance when foreign troops invade, or no one taking responsibility for the loss of territory. The meeting cannot express uniformity on such policies and situations. (2) Regarding the reform plan of the central system, Representative Sun is requested to prepare a concrete plan and submit it for discussion at tomorrow's (i.e., today's) meeting. (3) The fourth meeting will be held at 9:00 AM on October 30th.

Representatives Sent Telegrams of Condolence for Gu's Death　The Beijing and Guangdong representatives sent telegrams of condolence yesterday for the death of Gu Yingfen, saying: (1) To the Extraordinary Conference of the Central Executive and Supervisory Committee in Guangzhou: Upon receiving the telegram, we were shocked to learn that Mr. Gu Xiangqin passed away at 6:00 PM on the 28th. Times are difficult, and the overall situation is uncertain. The sudden death of a senior and experienced person is deeply painful. We send this telegram to express our condolences and hope for your compassion. Wang Zhaoming, Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, Wu Chaoshu, Chen Youren, Zou Lu, sincerely. (2) To Mr. Chen Bonan in Guangzhou: Convey to Mrs. Gu Xiangqin our condolences upon receiving the news of Mr. Xiangqin's death. The nation is in distress, and the sudden death of a senior and experienced person leaves the country in mourning. We have shared hardships and deeply mourn. We offer our condolences. Li Yu, Zhang Ji, Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Renjie, Chen Mingshu, sincerely. (3) To Mrs. Gu and siblings at the Gu residence on Cangbian Street in Guangzhou: We are deeply saddened by Mr. Xiangweng's passing, both from a public and private perspective. We hope you will restrain your grief and accept the changes. We send this telegram to offer our condolences and hope for your consideration. Li Wenfan, Zou Lu, Wu Chaoshu, Chen Youren, Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, sincerely.

Issue of System Change　Yesterday morning, at the third preparatory meeting, when Wu Chaoshu proposed an explanation of the "so-called uniformity in foreign affairs," after discussion and decision by the participants, the representatives at the meeting all believed that the preparatory meeting should promptly discuss important issues, and the others, which were secondary, could be left for later discussion. Therefore, the fifth item of the seven principles proposed by the Guangdong side, namely, the "Reform Plan of the Central System," was brought forward for discussion. As a result, Sun Zhesheng was publicly recommended to prepare a concrete plan and submit it to the fourth meeting for further discussion. After the meeting adjourned, this newspaper's reporter, considering that this case was of great importance to the central administrative system, specially visited Mr. Sun Zhesheng and was received. The following is a summary of his reform opinions on this case. Mr. Sun said, "I believe that the current central system grants too much power to the chairman. Therefore, I advocate reforming the current central system by imitating the nature of the cabinet systems of Germany and France, that is, to establish a 'National Government Committee' composed of members of the National Government, and still have a chairman of the National Government who represents the country externally and exercises political power internally. In other words, the National Government Committee is the same as the parliaments of Germany and France, and the chairman of the National Government is the same as the presidents of Germany and France, but the name is still chairman and not president. As for the president of the Executive Yuan, he is similar to the prime ministers of Germany and France and must be responsible to the National Government Committee." At this point, the reporter asked, "Then will the other four yuan be changed?" Mr. Sun replied, "The other four yuan will not be changed, but in fact, the focus of the five yuan's functions and implementation is still on the Executive Yuan. Therefore, it is very important that the Executive Yuan be responsible to the National Government Committee." The reporter asked whether the chairman of the National Government could still concurrently serve as the president of the Executive Yuan, and how the candidates for the chairman of the National Government and the members of the National Government would be produced. Mr. Sun replied that, according to the German and French systems, the members of the National Government should be elected by the people of the whole country, and this point still needs to be considered. However, the chairman of the National Government should be publicly recommended by all members of the National Government. As for the number of members of the National Government, it will naturally increase in the future, but the number is still to be discussed. The reporter asked whether the current Central Political Conference would continue to exist after the central system is reformed according to this proposal. Mr. Sun replied, "Of course, there is no need for the Central Political Conference to exist anymore, because the National Government Committee is the highest political organ in the country." The reporter asked, "What is your opinion on the abolition of the commander-in-chief?" Mr. Sun replied, "I advocate abolition, because under the National Government, the Ministry of Military Affairs and the General Staff Headquarters are jointly responsible for military affairs. Therefore, it seems unnecessary to establish a commander-in-chief in peacetime. As for declaring war on foreign countries, it is of course necessary to establish one for the convenience of command." The reporter asked, "Have you discussed party affairs in the meetings these days?" Mr. Sun replied, "No." The reporter asked, "In your opinion, when will the preparatory meeting be completed?" Mr. Sun replied, "It will probably be completed soon." At this point, another guest arrived, and the reporter took his leave.

Hu Visited Wang and Wu　Hu Hanmin suddenly suffered from abdominal pain the day before yesterday and was cured by Dr. Deng Zhende. Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, representatives from the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Water and Electricity Workers' Union, among others, visited Hu's residence. Wang Jingwei, Wu Chaoshu, and others were present. Hu, Wang, and others went out to meet them and talked for a long time. Hu felt quite tired. At that time, he happened to receive a telegram from Guangdong informing him of the death of Gu Yingfen. Hu had a deep personal relationship with Gu and was extremely saddened, even to the point of fainting. He was quickly treated by a doctor and recovered after about an hour. Yesterday afternoon at about 3:00 PM, Hu, accompanied by Li Wenfan, visited Wang Jingwei at 157 Seymour Road and talked for about two hours. Until about 5:00 PM, Hu and Li went together to Wu's residence on Gordon Road to attend a banquet.

Declaration of the Eight District Party Departments　The eight district party departments of this city, including the first, second, fifth, sixth, eighth, ninth, and tenth districts, expressed serious opinions on the current situation yesterday and issued a declaration, saying: "At a time when the nation is in deep distress and foreign aggression is imminent, and the danger to the nation's survival is imminent, all comrades of our party should uphold the spirit of defending the country against foreign enemies and unite to jointly resist foreign aggression, eliminate internal conflicts, and increase the nation's strength. This is the attitude that our party comrades should have in loving the party and saving the country, and it is also what the people of the whole country earnestly expect from the party. However, the way to save the country is even more urgent than putting out a fire. In the face of national crisis, our party comrades should be ready to fight at any moment, and there is no time for lengthy discussions and arguments. If saving the country is the premise, then any personal opinions can be sacrificed, any misunderstandings can be avoided, and there is no need for any form of meeting or any bargaining of conditions. If we treat each other with sincerity, then everyone can be forgiven. If we act with impartiality, then there is no room for exploitation. As for the central political system, it is related to the organization of our party, and the system of our party is based on the due process of laws and regulations, which cannot be easily changed. The reason why the previous special committee did not meet the expectations of the public was that it tampered with the party's laws and regulations. If we repeat the same mistakes, then we will only make things worse. Therefore, today, the only way is to concentrate the talents within the party on the existing central system and strengthen the political power, which is the most important task for saving the country at present. Moreover, when the diplomatic situation is increasingly isolated, if we change the central system and rashly change the international status, it will not only contradict the desire to resist Japan and save the country, but also go against the original intention of our advanced comrades to unite against foreign aggression. Since the foundation of our party is based on public opinion, all our actions should be in accordance with public opinion. Today, what the people expect from our party is that our party comrades can eliminate regionalism and unite unconditionally to confront foreign aggression. It is only when we regard the demands of the Guangzhou side as the starting point for cultivating democratic politics. Otherwise, we will only focus on petty gains and losses and waste time in endless disputes, ignoring the country's crisis and foreign aggression. How can we save the country from imminent danger? How can we meet the expectations of the people? And the so-called democratic politics will only become an empty slogan to deceive people. Therefore, today's affairs have no more urgent task than saving the country, and no more important issue than dealing with foreign aggression. We should quickly unite sincerely, join hands to enter Beijing, and devote all our efforts to saving the country and resisting foreign aggression, which is the only way out for all advanced comrades. As for political organization and national construction, we should firmly adhere to the Prime Minister's outline for national construction as the only fundamental code of law. The imperfections of personnel have nothing to do with the laws and regulations themselves. It is not to value people but to value laws and regulations. Even if there are good laws and systems, without people who abide by and implement the laws and regulations, they are equal to empty words and waste paper. Therefore, the key to governance lies not in the laws but in the people. We should restrain people to abide by the laws, not change the laws to accommodate people. Only by abiding by the laws can we promote the transition from rule by people to rule by law. Only rule by law can guarantee the realization of democratic politics. Otherwise, valuing people over the law will not only be a disguised form of dictatorship, but also a major obstacle to democratic politics. The gains and losses in this are of great importance. One mistake will affect the whole situation. We hope that the people of the country will learn from this."

Declaration of Various Trade Unions in This City　(Titles Omitted) Since the revolution, due to different political views, chaos and disasters have followed one after another, and there has been no peaceful year. The suffering of the people of the whole country is no less than in the era of warlords, which is very regrettable. It was hoped that after the success of the revolution, the political situation would gradually become peaceful, and all of the Prime Minister's proposals for peace and the genuine liberation of the people could be realized one by one. However, the selfish views of power have not been eliminated, and the political situation is even more unstable. Internal strife has led to foreign aggression. The Japanese imperialists, who have been watching for a long time but have not dared to act, have now dared to carry out their great violence. Therefore, our so-called revolutionary government should regard this as a deep hatred and humiliation. Therefore, if our party comrades still do not abandon their personal views and jointly face the national crisis at this time, it is unknown what kind of heart they have. Fortunately, all parties have deeply realized their mistakes and repented. The sincerity of all parties in regretting their mistakes is not without hope for the future of the Republic of China. However, to resist foreign aggression, we must first stabilize the country. To stabilize the country, we must first advocate war. The results of years of civil war have clearly shown us that the dream of military force is not achievable, and the Prime Minister's proposal for peaceful struggle is almost the only way to save China. Only with peace can we achieve unity, and only with genuine peace can we expect the sympathy of the whole country. This peaceful conference has brought together all parties. If all parties can meet each other with sincerity, it will be a great plan for saving the country and will be recognized by the people. We hope that the representatives will do their best to eliminate their prejudices, show accommodation, and make concessions. In the future, all party, government, and military affairs should follow the Prime Minister's teachings, re-establish policies, and implement them carefully. It is hoped that in the cooperation between the two sides, all kinds of disputes can be resolved, and then we can strive to revitalize and unite against foreign aggression. We must have the determination to break the cauldrons and sink the boats and go to the common goal without hesitation. The national crisis is imminent, and we will not resign until death. This is what all parties are responsible for today, and it is also what the people are eagerly hoping for. Indeed, at this critical moment, the survival of the country is at stake. If the country survives, we will all survive. If the country perishes, we will all perish. The people of the whole country will never ignore those who outwardly advocate peace but secretly plot destruction, or even use resistance against foreign aggression as a facade while actually having ulterior motives. They will not only be the public enemy of the people of the whole country, but also the sinners of China for all ages. We hereby declare this together with the people of the country. Shanghai Chinese Merchants' Ships Dismiss Japanese Crew Members 136

Jing Shun Steamer Begins

Haitong Dismisses Japanese Seafarers　The Jing Shun Steamer of Haitong Steamer Company in this port uses six Japanese crew members, including the captain, first mate, second mate, and chief engineer. Since the recent invasion of our national territory by the violent Japanese, the Chinese people have unanimously carried out an economic boycott against Japan. The company has also dismissed the hired captain, first mate, second mate, and other personnel. Since there is no contract restriction, the agreement can be terminated at any time. The Jing Shun Steamer arrived in Shanghai from Haizhou yesterday. After entering the Huai River, it stopped at Pier 31 to unload cargo. The company then notified the Japanese to immediately leave their posts and disembark.

Chinese Personnel Take Over, Dispute Arises　Before the Japanese crew members were dismissed, the company had already hired Hu Xiyuan as the captain and hired Huang Duncai, Chen Rongsheng, and others as chief and second engineers. They were scheduled to take over their duties on the ship yesterday afternoon. However, after the new captain arrived on the ship, a major dispute arose when Huang and Chen boarded the ship. The Nanjing Marine Engineering Association did not allow Huang and others to serve as chief and second engineers, saying that the association should send people to fill the posts. Huang and Chen argued that they were appointed by Haitong and approved by the Navigation Administration Bureau. Neither side would give way, and the engine room almost wanted to resolve the matter by force. The new captain, fearing that the Japanese had not yet left the ship and that this would provoke an incident, or that the Japanese would refuse to hand over their duties on the pretext, which would inevitably lead to disputes, persuaded Huang and others to report to the Navigation Bureau for resolution.

Petition the Navigation Bureau for Disposition　After Huang Duncai and Chen Rongsheng left, the Marine Engineering Association, without waiting for the order of the Navigation Bureau, immediately appointed He Shengcai and Cai Xuenian to board the ship and take over the positions of chief and second engineers. Huang and Chen immediately took the Haitong appointment letter and the registration certificate from the Navigation Bureau to report to the Navigation Administration Bureau and requested a ruling. At that time, Director Xi Zhongmou happened to be out, and they were instructed to go to the Bureau this morning to discuss the matter. It has been verified that Haitong Steamer is the first ship in Shanghai to dismiss Japanese crew members and replace them with Chinese crew members. From today onwards, if any Chinese merchant ships employ Japanese personnel and do not dismiss them, they will not be allowed to sail. This intention has been notified to all steamer bureaus for their information.

Anti-Japanese Association Holds Two Meetings

Executive Committee Meeting　The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of this city convened its eleventh executive committee meeting at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce meeting room at 4:00 PM yesterday, chaired by Wang Xiaolai and recorded by Yi Yikang. The meeting was held as scheduled. The proceedings of the meeting are recorded below: (1) Discussion on the Source Lai Foreign Firm's application for reconsideration of the flour case, which was submitted by the Standing Committee. Resolution: Eleven members, including Li Cishan, Wang Pingnan, Chen Yafo, Hu Fengxiang, Gu Ruofeng, Wang Changyuan, Chu Huiseng, Zheng Chengqing, Wang Xiliang, Ren Jinpin, and Zhu Xuefan, were appointed to review whether the new evidence submitted by the Source Lai Firm has the value of proposing a reconsideration. The previous resolution to confiscate the flour for disaster relief should be communicated to the Relief Committee to temporarily suspend its use. Resolution: Five members, including Yu Hualong, Li Cishan, Hu Fengxiang, Li Yongxiang, and Wang Pingnan, were appointed to review the matter, and Yu Hualong was designated to convene the meeting. (3) Should the resignation of Committee Member Hu Shuhua from the position of Standing Committee Member be approved? Resolution: Approved. Committee Member Chu Huiseng was appointed to fill the vacancy. (4) Committee Member Ren Jinpin proposed that the Association should hold a regular meeting to welcome the peace representatives to express the Association's position. Resolution: Referred to the Standing Committee for handling. (5) The Lun Chang Company sent a letter requesting a solution to the ordering method. Resolution: The reply was not approved.

Standing Committee Meeting　The Anti-Japanese Association convened its fourteenth standing committee meeting at the Standing Committee Room of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce at 2:00 PM yesterday. The firm requested that the matter be examined and decided. Resolution: Submitted to the Executive Committee. (2) The Coal Industry and Charcoal Industry Anti-Japanese Association sent a letter stating that its member, Yang Zuyong, privately sold charcoal to Japanese merchants and dared to openly offer bribes during the inspection. He has now been detained by the Association, and a request is made for verification. How should the matter be handled? Resolution: Yang Zuyong was released on bail, the bribe was confiscated for public use, and the case was referred to the Disciplinary Committee. (3) Lawyer Wu Youyuan sent a letter asking whether a Japanese land deed is valid and requested instructions. Resolution: The reply was that it was rejected. Resolution: Investigated and replied. (5) The Shanghai Inspection Association sent a letter asking to first seal the Japanese goods and nitrate mines of the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Provincial Nitrate Mining Bureau, and then seal the Japanese goods and nitrate mines of various factories. How should the matter be handled? Resolution: Seal as requested. (6) The Pudong Inspection Office reported that Japanese soldiers landed, looted goods, and stabbed an inspector. How should the matter be handled? Resolution: Submit a protest to the Municipal Government.

Silk and Satin Industry Seriously Investigates Japanese Goods

Non-Members Limited to Three Days to Report for Inspection

The Shanghai Silk and Satin Industry Association has been conducting inspections of Japanese goods in the silk and satin industry since the 15th of this month. Teams have been working continuously without interruption. As of yesterday, all member stores have been inspected. However, among the non-member businesses, only a few have reported for inspection since the announcement was published in the newspaper. It is reported that the association, in order to solemnly fulfill its inspection responsibilities and protect the interests of the industry, convened its eighth inspection team meeting yesterday, with Jiang Fengshao publicly elected as chairman to discuss various cases. (1) Standing Committee Member Luo Qinghua proposed that non-member businesses with remaining Japanese goods should be given an extension of three days to register with the association for inspection and sealing. If they still fail to report for inspection after the deadline, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association will be notified to handle the matter, and the inspected businesses and past work will be reported to the Committee for the Economic Boycott of Japan under the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce for verification. Is a public decision requested? Resolution: Passed. (2) If any inspection committee member has leave, regardless of the length of the leave, they should entrust a representative to attend the meeting in order to emphasize their responsibilities. Resolution: Passed. (3) If any Japanese goods have already been sealed by the association, but some have been missed, they should be reported to the association within one day so that personnel can be dispatched to conduct a supplementary inspection. Resolution: Passed.

Second General Meeting of the YMCA Members 138

The YMCA Members Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held its first general meeting at the Shanghai YMCA auditorium at 5:30 pm on the 28th. The presiding group consisted of Gu Zhiling, Tan Bozhi, and Peng Zunlu, with approximately a thousand people in attendance. Yin Zhiling delivered the opening address. Wang Zaoshi gave a speech on "The Unification Conference and the Future of China." Tan Bozhi reported on the association's activities. Ren Zuojun reported on the economic plan. Mai delivered a speech on "Concrete Measures for Anti-Japanese National Salvation." Subsequently, a public discussion was held. The association reached a resolution to issue a circular telegram regarding its important propositions and work concerning the serious current situation. The meeting adjourned at 8:00 pm. The full text of the circular telegram is recorded below: "The Japanese have long coveted Manchuria and Mongolia, and are actively preparing to encroach on China. They threaten to seize Taiwan, forcibly occupy Dalian, and coerce us into signing the Twenty-One Demands of the fourth year of the Republic. Through enticements and cunning schemes, they collude with warlords and incite internal strife. Their viciousness and cruelty arouse the indignation of both heaven and man. Yet, our government and people, both high and low, turn a blind eye. We haggle over trivial gains and losses, and make no substantial preparations for self-defense. Calamities arise one after another. We resort to slogans and banners to confront violence. When the enemy arrives, we are ordered to surrender and disarm as a matter of course. If this is how a nation is governed, how can it escape natural selection? Now, the Japanese are intensifying their aggression. Their troops are approaching the key cities of Guanzhong. The state of affairs is critical. Survival is uncertain. Yet, the officials in charge in the North and South continue to vacillate in peace talks, using empty words on paper as their banner, without any practical methods for saving the nation. Could it be that they believe the party and the nation can be separate, and that the party can survive even if the nation perishes? Our association, as patriotic citizens, witnessing the national crisis looming and the danger of national destruction, in addition to following the lead of other national salvation associations, unanimously urge the government to quickly unify the nation and prepare to resist foreign aggression. Regarding this Japanese military aggression, we have resolved to issue five propositions as follows, hoping for public awareness: (1) The people of the whole country, regardless of party affiliation, should concentrate talent and unite to resist aggression. (2) Anyone who exploits the national crisis to advance their private interests should be considered a public enemy of the nation. (3) No one is allowed to conclude secret treaties with Japan that sacrifice national sovereignty. Violators will be deemed guilty of treason. (4) Before the complete withdrawal of Japanese troops, we insist on opposing direct negotiations. (5) The government's diplomacy with Japan should be based on the will of the people and announce its policies publicly."

Yesterday, the Zhonghua Book Company Resumed Work 140

The Minzhi Book Company Continues Its Work Stoppage.

The Municipal Government Scheduled to Convene Arbitration.

After all the employees of the Zhonghua and Minzhi Book Companies went on strike, the employees of Zhonghua followed the order and resumed work yesterday. Minzhi continued its work stoppage yesterday. The Social Affairs Bureau ordered Minzhi yesterday to comply with the previous order and allow Jin Shifa to resume work. The details of each situation are recorded separately below. Zhonghua Resumes Work.

The Publishing Industry Association, in order to comply with the order, accompanied Li Hongbin, a worker from the Zhonghua Book Company, to resume work at 7:00 am yesterday. It also persuaded all the employees of the general factory and distribution office to work as usual. As a result, all the employees immediately stopped the work stoppage and worked as usual. However, Tu Jinshi, the deputy director of the general factory printing office, had to consult with the general manager regarding Li Hongbin's resumption of work. It is reported that after Li Hongbin entered the letterpress printing department, the capital side did not assign him any work. All the employees were very angry when they heard the news.

Notice to Employees. The Zhonghua Book Company, after a resolution by the board of directors, announced to all employees yesterday: The council resolved in a meeting that it will report to the Social Affairs Bureau for investigation and handling the situation of a small number of workers and shop assistants forcing a work stoppage and preventing customers from entering the store. If it is absolutely necessary, legal remedies may be sought. In addition, it received a letter from 53 people at the main store asking how wages would be paid in the future for those who did not participate in the work stoppage. After deliberation, the council decided that: (1) Those who did not participate in the work stoppage and worked as usual will be paid their wages as usual. (2) Those who participated in the work stoppage will not be paid their wages. (3) Those who did not want to participate in the work stoppage but were forced to not work should notify the department head or section chief to register, and wages will be paid as usual after verification.

Order from the Social Affairs Bureau. All the workers of the Minzhi Book Company continued to strike yesterday. The Publishing Industry Association received an order from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, which stated roughly: In order to comply with the order, the case of the Minzhi Book Company dismissing worker Jin Shifa, in addition to ordering the bureau to comply with the previous order, it is ordered that it be obeyed and that all workers be instructed to quickly resume work as usual. This order is crucial. The association immediately convened a meeting to discuss how to proceed.

Submission from the Chamber of Commerce. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce submitted a letter to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau regarding the work stoppage of the Zhonghua Book Company employees, stating roughly that the case originated from a mutual fight between worker Li Hongbin and a comrade in the same machine. In order to stabilize business and avoid disputes, the employer dismissed him as usual. The person concerned had no objection. Later, a cadre of the Publishing Industry Association raised an objection and reported to the bureau, requesting reinstatement. After approval, he was given a demerit and allowed to resume work. The printing office of the company replied that it had not received an order from the company and would notify it after the board of directors made a decision. The employer did not refuse reinstatement. However, the cadre of the union did not comply with Article 23 of the Labor Union Law and forcibly instigated a strike. When it failed, he instigated the shop assistants to stage a work stoppage and sent people to the store to obstruct customers. Such arbitrary obstruction of the company's business caused the company to invoke Articles 27, Section 1 and 7 of the Labor Union Law or Article 74 of the Factory Law and other provisions, requesting severe punishment in accordance with the law. It is appropriate to submit a request to the bureau for review and approval and to take legal action.

Petition from Representatives. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce believed that the workers' work stoppage was a disguised strike and should be prohibited by the party and government organs. The Standing Committee decided to publicly recommend Committee Members Ye Huijun and Zhu Wenqi to go to the Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Headquarters, and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to request that it be stopped.

Order from the Party Headquarters. It is reported that the Municipal Party Headquarters has strictly ordered the Publishing Industry Workers' Union to instruct the workers of the two book companies to resume work immediately and await mediation. The document stated: For the strict enforcement of the order, it is reported that the workers of the Zhonghua and Minzhi Book Companies went on strike due to the failure to reach an agreement with the capital side on the terms and conditions of labor and capital. In view of the current national crisis and the urgency of foreign aggression, both labor and capital should unite and not engage in disputes. The Zhonghua and Minzhi Book Companies workers are ordered to comply with the case. They should immediately instruct the workers to resume work immediately. All disputes over the terms and conditions should be resolved through mediation in accordance with the law, and should not be resisted or delayed, so as not to cause inconvenience. This order is crucial.

Scheduled Arbitration. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau declared that mediation of the Zhonghua Book Company's employees' treatment conditions was unsuccessful and submitted it to the Municipal Government for arbitration. Yesterday, the Shanghai Municipal Labor and Capital Arbitration Committee notified both labor and capital, stating that the committee is scheduled to arbitrate the case of the Zhonghua Book Company's labor demands for improved treatment at 1:00 pm on Saturday, October 31st. Representatives are requested to appear on time to state their views and await arbitration. This notice is issued by Chairman and Committee Member Sun Baorong.

Because it hinders the prospects for resisting Japan.

Although the Tram is Running After the Electric Company's Work Stoppage, Tickets are Not Sold. 143

The Public Security Bureau Sends Police to Protect the Traffic.

The Party Headquarters Mediation Has a Concrete Solution.

The Staff Will Meet and May Resume Work This Morning.

After the work stoppage of all the staff of the Municipal Chinese Electric Company, the Social Affairs Bureau strictly ordered it to be stopped and reported it to the Municipal Government, which quickly summoned a public decision. The Municipal Party Headquarters took on the task of mediation, and it is reported that there are concrete measures. Although the tram ran as usual yesterday, the ticket sales were stopped. The Public Security Bureau sent police to protect it. The details of each situation are recorded below.

Tram Blocked. After all the staff went on strike for the terms and conditions of treatment the day before yesterday, the staff of the traffic department immediately stopped arranging shifts, stopping the car, and issuing tickets. As a result, all the workers of the traffic department went to work yesterday morning, but no one was assigned work and no tickets could be sold. They had no choice but to stand in the company and wait for work. The tram was originally scheduled to leave the factory at 5:45 am, but as a result, it did not leave the factory until 7:00 am.

Protect the Traffic. Chen Xizeng, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, heard that the Chinese tram was suspended due to the staff's work stoppage. In order to maintain traffic and social order, he ordered the Second District Police Station to send a patrol officer from the Gaochangmiao Police Station to the Electric Company to persuade them to run as usual to facilitate traffic. Therefore, at 7:30 am, the trams on all routes started to leave the factory. Drivers sold tickets and worked on the same shift as the day before. However, no one issued tickets, so they had to run the tram without selling tickets. The Public Security Bureau sent more than 20 armed policemen from the Police Brigade and eight armed policemen from the Second District to distribute to the car for protection.

Traffic Situation. Yesterday, the Chinese trams ran nine vehicles on Route 1 from Xiaodongmen to Gaochangli, four vehicles on Route 2 from Xiaodongmen to Ximen, eight vehicles on Route 3 with trailers, and six vehicles on Route 4 from Ximen to Gaochangmiao. Because there were no tickets sold in the car, the general public was happy to take the ride. As a result, the number of passengers increased several times compared to the past, and the trams were crowded. In order to avoid danger, the speed was slightly slower, and a group of naughty children occupied the car for fun. The business of public buses and rickshaws was greatly affected.

Municipal Government Investigation. After the Municipal Government received the Social Affairs Bureau's report on the handling of the Chinese Electric staff's treatment conditions, the Mayor was deeply concerned that the dispute would expand and affect the transportation industry and social order. In order to resolve it quickly, he specially sent Xu Ji and Xiu to investigate the truth and persuade the staff to work as usual and await legal processing.

Party Headquarters Mediation. In order to quickly resolve the Chinese staff's work stoppage, the Municipal Party Headquarters, in addition to sending personnel to investigate the truth, invited representatives of all the staff and company representatives to mediate by Standing Committee Wu Kaixian and Xu Yefu, Minister of Civil Training, the night before yesterday. It started at 8:00 pm and did not end until 2:00 am this morning. The result was very satisfactory. This morning at 10:00 am, mediation will continue. It is reported that by 3:00 pm, there has been a considerable solution. Company Losses. Since the work stoppage of all the staff, the Chinese Electric Company, in addition to convening a temporary emergency meeting, General Manager Lu Bohong and Director Gu Xinyi went to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to submit everything at 10:00 am yesterday morning. It is reported that the company lost more than 2,500 yuan yesterday when the tram ran without selling tickets. Moreover, everything else is not included.

General Assembly. Since the Municipal Party Headquarters took on the task of mediation, there has been a concrete solution. The representatives of all the staff held a temporary emergency meeting at the China National Products Road Staff Liaison Office of the Chinese Electric Company in Nanshi at 6:00 pm yesterday to discuss the solution. It did not end until 9:00 pm. It is reported that work may resume this morning.

The Third Batch of Personnel from the Shenyang Arsenal Arrives in Shanghai 145

The Relief Committee Scheduled to Issue Relief Funds

The third batch of personnel from the Shenyang Arsenal has arrived in Shanghai and organized a maintenance group to appeal to various agencies. The National Government Relief Committee has scheduled to issue relief funds to the second batch of personnel. As for the first batch of personnel, due to lack of livelihood, it was decided to petition again. The details of each situation are recorded below.

Third Batch Arrives in Shanghai. On October 26, the Zhao Dian Company's Hexing ship arrived in Shanghai, followed by the third batch of 126 personnel from the Shenyang Arsenal who escaped to Shanghai and temporarily resided in the Qu Zhenren Temple in Gaochangmiao. Ji Zhiqingyuan maintains that the third group dispatched representatives Lin Huiqing and others to the National Government Relief Committee to request to maintain their current livelihood the day before yesterday. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency knocked on the door of the third batch of victims to inquire about the recent situation in Shenyang. It is reported that most of the shops in Shenyang have opened for business, but the business is sparse. The Japanese soldiers are monitoring the people's movements very strictly and prohibiting gatherings of more than three people. They also hire Chinese workers to disassemble all the machinery of the factory and load it to Dalian. All the machinery of the factory has been moved out, and the losses are estimated to be over 100 million.

Issue Relief Funds. After the second batch of 260 victims arrived in Shanghai, the National Government Relief Committee has scheduled to send personnel from the National Public Security Bureau and the Social Affairs Bureau to distribute relief funds on October 31, with four yuan per person. The relief funds collected by the first batch of victims have long been exhausted, and they are currently lacking in livelihood. The Municipal Government has telegraphed the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs requesting resettlement, but has not yet received a reply. Therefore, they are preparing to dispatch representatives to petition.

Pacific Society Telegraphs to Invite Soviet Representatives to Attend the Meeting 146

It Is Feared That They Will Not Be Able to Attend This Session.

The Zi Lin Bao reported that when the Pacific Society met on Wednesday afternoon, it unanimously decided to allow the Soviet Union to formally join the society and telegraphed that night to invite a representative to attend the meeting to discuss everything. This matter has been discussed by the society and Soviet scientific groups for a long time. The acting secretary-general of the society, Lumis, has been to Moscow several times in recent years to discuss with Russian representatives. When the society met in Xijing in 1929, a Russian observer was present. Since then, Russian scientific and cultural groups have paid attention to the activities of the society and organized the Pacific Committee. The society is now telegraphing the committee to invite representatives to join the discussion. However, it is too late this year, and they will not be able to attend. According to Lumis, the committee has no relationship with Soviet political activities, and most of its members are not communists. At the society's discussion on Wednesday, attention was focused on the Manchurian issue, and Chinese and Japanese representatives debated fiercely. Hua Junchi, the private secretary of the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Drummond, was also present as an observer. Mr. Hua arrived in Shanghai from Europe specifically for this matter.

Urgent Fundraising for Winter Relief 149

Allocation of Winter Relief Quotas to Various Provinces

The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief for Flood Victims in Various Provinces held its 74th regular meeting yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. Attendees included Huang Hanzhi, Ma Youfeng, Qu Wenliu, Xu Shiying, Yu Zhi'ang, Li Zhian, Du Yuesheng, Wang Ting, Zhu Ziqiao, Zhang Gongheng, Jin Guanfu, Wu Zhijuan, Zhang Zhijiang (representing Weng Guoxun), Qian Junren, Ha Shaofu, Wang Xiaolai, and others. They elected Xu Shiying as chairman and Yang Jichun as recorder. First, Zhang Gongheng, special commissioner for disaster relief in southern Anhui, reported on the disaster relief situation in seven counties in southern Anhui. Then, Li Ji, special commissioner for disaster relief in Hubei, reported on the recent situation of disaster relief and recommended Zhou Xingtang as the special commissioner for disaster relief in Hubei in his place. Next, the following proposals were discussed and resolved: (1) The previous regular meeting resolved that the standing committee members would immediately determine emergency winter relief measures. Now that a plan has been drafted, it was approved. (2) You Xiwun, representative of the Huangyan Rice Industry Association, offered to handle 20,000 bags of relief rice for the committee at a price reduced by two yuan from the current lowest rice price in Shanghai. The resolution was temporarily reserved. (3) Xu Guozhi telegraphed that nine porridge kitchens must be established in central Anhui immediately, each requiring at least tens of thousands of yuan. Whether to set up more will be considered after the relief workers have submitted complete reports. (4) Xu Guohuai telegraphed detailed plans for winter relief in central Anhui, where over 3.9 million people in 15 disaster-stricken counties need relief. Distributing 20% of the relief funds would require over 780,000 yuan, and distributing 10% in winter clothing would require over 390,000 sets of cotton clothes. How to approve this request? (5) The Shaanxi Provincial Relief Association telegraphed that the weather is getting colder and winter relief is imminent. They propose setting up porridge kitchens in severely affected areas and request funds. (6) The Relief Association received a telegram from the Guizhou Chinese and Foreign Relief Association stating that the counties along the Yuan and Zhu rivers in that province have suffered severely and requesting relief. It was resolved that the above four proposals be handled under winter relief. (7) The Anhui Provincial Relief Association sent a letter with plans for flood relief, including emergency relief, agricultural relief, and industrial relief, and requested additional assistance. The resolution was passed. (8) The total amount of requests for industrial relief from various locations has exceeded ten million yuan. The committee is unable to handle this, and the funds needed for relief and seeds alone would require tens of thousands of yuan per province. Each province also needs hundreds of thousands of sets of cotton clothes. The committee's relief income is gradually decreasing. How should we raise funds? The resolution was handed over to the fundraising group. (9) The current allocation of relief funds to various provinces is inevitably skewed based on requests. More requests result in more allocation, and no requests result in no allocation, which is unfair. Now that the disaster situation in each province is generally clear, it is proposed to establish concrete measures based on the actual situation to avoid favoring some and neglecting others. The resolution was to calculate the distribution of the two winter emergency relief funds as a percentage, with Anhui receiving 15%, Jiangsu and Hubei each receiving 12%, Henan, Hunan, and Jiangxi each receiving 10%, Zhejiang receiving 4%, Guizhou receiving 3%, and Shandong, Shaanxi, Gansu, and other provinces totaling 24%. (10) A letter from the publicity group. It was resolved to invite Xu Jingren, Zhu Ziqiao, Li Zuli, and Weng Guoxun to negotiate. (11) A letter from Sa Zhenbing of Fujian stating that he was honored to be appointed as an executive member and special commissioner for disaster relief by the committee, but felt unable to shoulder such a heavy responsibility. However, he could try his best within the Ningde and Gutian areas. The resolution was to send a letter requesting his hard work. (12) A letter from the Shanghai Municipal Association of Traditional Chinese Medicine stating that the association is responsible for diagnosis and medication at the disaster relief shelters, and this will continue in the future. They request the committee to provide subsidies for medication in the future. The resolution was to approve the subsidy.

Winter Emergency Relief Rules Passed

The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief for Flood Victims in Various Provinces passed 16 articles of rules for handling winter emergency relief at its meeting yesterday. The original text is as follows: (1) Each province will have one chief director, named "Chief Director of the Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief for Flood Victims in Various Provinces for XX Province." (Referred to as "the Committee" below) The chief director will be responsible for relief in various counties of that province. The relief workers dispatched will be named "Relief Director of the Committee for XX Province, XX County." (2) The chief director will be hired by the Committee, and the directors of each province will be recommended by the chief director and hired by the Committee. (3) The Committee will issue each provincial chief director a seal, with the inscription "Seal of the Chief Director of the Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Emergency Relief for Flood Victims in XX Province." The seal used by the county directors will be inscribed "Seal of the Relief Director of the Committee for XX Province, XX County." The style will be determined by the Committee and issued locally by the provincial chief director, with a report to the Committee for record. (4) Relief tickets, flags, and armbands will be issued by the Committee to the chief director, who will distribute them to the county directors for use. (5) The Committee's relief efforts will focus on areas not covered by official relief or will be discussed and demarcated with official relief agencies in advance to achieve effective division of labor and cooperation, avoiding duplication and bias. (6) The provincial chief directors and county directors dispatched by the Committee will, in principle, not concurrently handle other relief work. However, if necessary, they must obtain the Committee's permission. (7) If other relief organizations wish to conduct relief work in the counties designated by the Committee, they may either demarcate areas within the county and conduct relief separately, or merge the relief funds into the Committee's relief funds for joint distribution. However, for joint distribution, the relief tickets must be stamped with the joint distribution mark of the XX relief organization. (8) When handling winter relief, the directors should conduct on-site surveys based on the local situation to determine whether seeds, cotton clothes, porridge kitchens, food, cash, or industrial relief are needed. The chief director will then report to the Committee for approval and implementation. (9) The investigation will be handled by the relief workers, and the relief funds should be handed over to the local county government and legal organizations to distribute the relief tickets and retain the stubs. The chief director will collect the stubs and submit them to the Committee. The relief tickets will be collected by the county government and sent back to the Committee along with the receipts for the relief funds distributed. (10) Since the Committee is a relief organization, it should follow the principles of strict investigation, lenient distribution, and saving the dying, not the poor. All other relief methods are printed in the book "Humble Opinions on Relief, Important Points on Relief," which is issued to all relief workers and handled according to past relief methods. (11) Each provincial office may employ two to four clerks to handle documents, general affairs, accounting, and inspection. However, the monthly living expenses should not exceed twenty yuan. Each county branch office may employ one or two clerks to handle internal affairs. However, the monthly living expenses should not exceed twenty yuan. (12) Relief expenses will be disbursed by the Committee to the relief workers when they depart. If the amount is insufficient, the chief director may request an increase. However, all relief expenses will be paid from the relief funds. Spending one extra penny means one less penny for the victims, and saving one penny means one more penny for the victims. Therefore, travel expenses can only be reduced according to the travel expense rules set by the Central Relief Commission and cannot be exceeded. (13) The procedures for disbursing funds must be complete to avoid objections from the Committee's audit team and accountants. (14) After departing, all staff members must report the progress of the relief efforts to the Committee at any time for assessment. (15) These rules will be implemented upon resolution by the Committee's standing committee.

(2) The Good Friends Society (Liangchen Hao You She) contributed 10% of its five-day business income during its 10th-anniversary price reduction period, totaling 50 yuan. Ling Sifei sold paintings to Lin Pingsun and obtained 5 yuan, which was also included. (3) A letter from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association stating that this amount is to be used for public funds. The association still needs to review it, so please postpone the use.

Large Batch of Disaster Victims from Mengcheng Arrives in Shanghai

Over 1,400 disaster victims from Mengcheng, Anhui, arrived in Nanjing by ship the day before yesterday. They set up tents on the open space in Xiaguan and stayed overnight. The next morning, they gathered and went to the Capital Flood Relief Association to request accommodation and relief. The association replied that it was currently in the process of dispersing refugees and that most of the shelters had already been closed. It was impossible to accommodate these disaster victims. Therefore, it sent personnel to negotiate with the Railway Bureau, which allocated ten cars. The Xiaguan Police Department dispatched police to escort them onto the cars and transport them to Shanghai. The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received a letter from the Capital Flood Relief Association stating that over 1,400 refugees from Mengcheng had been transported by train from Nanjing and were expected to arrive in Shanghai on the evening of the 29th. It requested that appropriate measures be taken to provide relief to these disaster victims. After receiving the letter, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau, instructing the nearby police stations to take care of the refugees when they arrive in Shanghai. It also sent letters to various charitable organizations to seek relief.

Letter Requesting the National Government to Allocate Relief Clothing

Huang Chunzhou, director of the Clothing Relief Association at 207 West Mandel Road, Racecourse, sent a letter to the National Government Flood Relief Committee yesterday, stating: "The clothing collected by our association, in addition to being sent to the Shanghai branch of the China Relief Association and your committee to accommodate disaster victims, has recently sent 5,000 pieces to the Hunan Provincial Government and 1,000 pieces to the Chongde Relief Association. Murderer Sentenced Due to Jealousy 150

Zhao Doushi Case Redressed

Zhao Qilang from Haimen had an affair with the widow Zhao Doushi. Later, Zhao Doushi also had an affair with Kong Qingrong, who lived on Miezha Street. Zhao, driven by jealousy, colluded with his fellow villager Wang Cailang to lure Kong to the Xiaoshadu Railway and kill him. They cut off the deceased's genitals and threw them on the tracks, trying to make it look like a train accident to cover up their crime. However, the local court discovered the truth during the autopsy and ordered the arrest of the murderers. Unexpectedly, Zhao Doushi's son secretly informed the police station, which led to the cracking of the case. Zhao Qilang, Wang Cailang, and others were subsequently sent to the court. After the prosecutor filed a public prosecution, the criminal court judge summoned and interrogated them. Yesterday, Judge Qian announced the judgment, sentencing Zhao Qilang to life imprisonment and Wang Cailang to ten years in prison as a warning.

Lawsuit Over Train Crash on Beijing-Shanghai Railway 151

Injured Passengers to Sue for Damages

The express train from Beijing to Shanghai on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway recently collided with a freight train in Zhenru, causing many injuries, as reported in the newspapers. The Shanghai lawyer Chen Zhigao, who was returning to Shanghai from Suzhou on the train to attend a court session, was also seriously injured in the head and went to the German Hospital for treatment. The doctor advised him to rest for three weeks before he could recover. At the same time, the passengers believed that the railway bureau's staff were negligent, leading to frequent train accidents. This time, over twenty passengers were injured. Furthermore, the railway bureau had not taken any remedial measures for the injured, making future travel extremely dangerous. This incident was a major fault due to the railway bureau's improper personnel management. The passengers suffered damages as a result and the railway bureau should be fully responsible. The damages to lawyer Chen, who had a busy law practice, were particularly significant. The passengers requested lawyer Chen to file a lawsuit against the railway bureau for damages to ensure future safety. Many of the injured also went to lawyer Chen's office at 96 Beijing Road to discuss joint litigation.

Commendable Bravery of Shop Employee in Apprehending Thief 152

Zhao Linfu, a 54-year-old man from Chaozhou, Guangdong, has been running the Sen Tai pawnshop at 40-42 Dongxinqiao Street (old address 145) in the French Concession for many years. The business has been doing well. After the reconstruction of the Baoyu Lane building opposite the shop, business has been booming. This attracted the attention of thieves. Yesterday morning at around 8:00 AM, as the shop was just opening and the employees were organizing the goods, an apprentice returned from fetching water. Unexpectedly, three thieves wearing short blue Yuan-style outfits, with one thief standing at the door as a lookout and two thieves holding guns, secretly followed the apprentice into the shop. They ordered the employees to remain silent and robbed cash and silver dollars from the drawers, totaling over 100 yuan. They left the shop and fled north. One of the shop employees, Zheng Guangyu, a 24-year-old man also from Chaozhou, was naturally alert. He saw the thieves leave the shop and secretly followed them. Zheng paid special attention to the thief in the short blue outfit who was holding the gun. When they reached Adora Road and turned west onto Xinxinqiao Street, then west along Caishi Street to the intersection of Mintiniyin Road and Jincheng Bank, the thief suddenly stopped, looked around nervously, as if waiting for someone. Seeing the opportunity, Zheng jumped on the thief from behind and grabbed him, shouting for help. Nearby detectives gathered and assisted in capturing the thief on the spot. They found a four-inch Browning pistol with eight bullets on the thief. They took him to the police station. After a detailed interrogation, the thief confessed that his name was Zhang Guiying, from Anhui, and that he was 36 years old. He admitted to colluding with others to commit robbery. He was immediately detained and will be sent to the court for severe punishment.

Appeal Case of Russian Man Ordering Military Supplies 153

Bick Attacks Laifa

Claims Ties to Noulens

The Russian man, Krilich Bick-Ravinsky, previously impersonated a military advisor to the National Government and, along with Zhang Faying, who claimed to be a procurement commissioner of the National Government, ordered military supplies worth about two million yuan from the Laifa Foreign Company, owned by the Englishman Laifa on Guangdong Road. They also forged documents to defraud Zhu Ziyao of money. Laifa reported this to the police station, which sent Bick and Ravinsky to the First Special District Court. Each was sentenced to one year in prison, as reported in previous newspapers. However, Bick refused to accept the sentence and hired lawyer Qiu Fenling to file an appeal with the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Song Yuan and two assessors, Gao and Ye, held a trial in the first criminal court. The police station was represented by lawyers Ru Baoyi and Li Zhishan. First, Bick stated the reasons for his dissatisfaction with the original judgment, claiming that he had no involvement in the case and had never been to the Laifa Foreign Company. Ravinsky gave him a contract for the military supplies ordered by Laifa and asked him to report it to the customs. If the customs intercepted the military supplies, they would receive a reward of 25 yuan per gun. Bick also claimed that he never impersonated a military advisor and was framed. He attacked Laifa's behavior, claiming that Laifa's business was improper and that he had a close relationship with the communist leader Noulens. All of Noulens' military supplies passed through Laifa. Fearing that he would reveal their secrets, Laifa had him arrested one day after Noulens was arrested. The presiding judge noted that the appellant, Laifa, was not present today and that the witnesses had not been gathered, so he adjourned the trial to a later date.

Extradited from Tianjin, Trial Held in Shanghai Yesterday
