Verdict in Burglary and Murder Case 155

Ma A'er Sentenced to Death

On the morning of September 19th, at 1:00 AM, the home of Zhu Yangshan, a Qingpu native, on the second floor of the Yichang Electrical Company at 196 East Seward Road, was burglarized. The thieves broke through the fence in the back and entered, stealing valuables worth over 1,000 yuan. They also killed Zhu's aunt-in-law, Gu Caoshi, and the maid, Zhou Lushi, with knives. Cai Zhitian, a Chinese detective from the Huishan Police Station, arrested the murderer, Ma A'er (who was his chauffeur), from Tongzhou, along with a knife. The First Special District Court interrogated them, as reported in previous newspapers. The case has now concluded and is awaiting sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Shen Bingrong held a trial in the third criminal court. The police station's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, instructed the police to bring Ma A'er to court. Judge Shen announced the verdict, sentencing Ma A'er to death for the crime of burglary and intentional homicide. The murder weapon was confiscated.

Butcher Sentenced to 15 Years for Killing His Wife 156

Qin Shoufan, a butcher from Haimen who worked at Chen Xinji's pig slaughterhouse at 55 Yuezhou Road, had a wife named Zhang (32 years old). Zhang was promiscuous and had an affair with a fellow villager surnamed Fan at 50 Jiaxing Road on the 11th of this month. Qin found out and on the morning of the 19th, at 11:30 AM, he found Zhang and took her to his brother's place at 3248 Zhoujiazui Road. He asked Zhang to hand over 30 yuan for travel expenses, but she refused. Qin became enraged and used a

Page 16

knife to stab Zhang three times in the legs and abdomen before fleeing. Zhang died from her injuries. The Harbin Police Station arrested Qin and sent him to the First Special District Court for interrogation. Yesterday morning, the police station sent Qin Shoufan to the third criminal court. Judge Shen Bingrong sentenced Qin Shoufan to 15 years in prison for the crime of murder. The number of days spent in custody before the judgment was finalized will be counted as one day of imprisonment for every two days.

City Chamber of Commerce Relief Meeting for Coal Shortage 157

Organized jointly by the Chamber of Commerce, Shipping Industry, and Coal Industry

A committee is formed

Measures from various industrial and commercial groups

The City Chamber of Commerce, in order to discuss the coal shortage problem, invited representatives from the Coal Industry and Shipping Industry Associations yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM for a joint meeting. Present were shipping representatives Zeng Guangqing, Min Xinwu, Chen Bogang, Yao Shumin, Ding Xijun, Chen Shuntong, Zhao Yunhe, and Chen Jisheng, and coal industry representatives Chen Qisheng, Mao Chunpu, Pan Yisan, Shen Jinzhou, Liu Hongsheng, and others. From the City Chamber of Commerce were Wang Xiaolai and Xu Jiying. Wang Xiaolai, as chairman, first presented the Coal Industry Association's letter stating that local coal reserves were low. Since the coal embargo after registration, the supply of national coal was urgently needed. However, due to the lack of additional vehicles and the shortage of state-owned shipping, a meeting was requested to express the urgent situation. Representatives from both industries were asked to attend and share their insights to avoid a coal shortage and to benefit the anti-Japanese effort. Representatives from both the coal and shipping industries then presented their opinions on the actual coal demand in Shanghai and the required number of ships. After detailed discussion, the shipping industry agreed to allocate its members' larger vessels for use. It was estimated that, in addition to the 120,000 tons already being shipped to Shanghai by hired vessels, the remaining shortfall could be transported by Chinese ships, ensuring no future coal shortage. Both parties were satisfied and immediately resolved to have the Chamber of Commerce, Shipping Industry, and Coal Industry each appoint three committee members to form a joint committee. It was decided that this committee would convene next Saturday at 3:00 PM at the Chamber to discuss further actions.

Two Telegrams from the City Chamber of Commerce. The City Chamber of Commerce and other groups yesterday sent two urgent telegrams regarding the coal shortage relief issue. The telegrams read: (1) To the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Premier and Minister of Industry Kong, Minister of Railways Lian, and Provincial Governor Han: Since the Jiaoji Railway announced a coal transportation price increase on November 1st, Shandong mine owners have resolved to strike on that day. We are aware that, in this small corner of the sea, Japanese coal is nearly exhausted, and Southern China relies on Northern mines for fuel. The Beipiao coal from Yingkou cannot be transported due to the Northern Ning Railway obstruction. The Jingxing and Datong coal from Tanggu cannot be heavily loaded due to the shallow winter waters. The Zhongxing coal from Jinpu is only for railway use, and the Liuhegou coal from Pinghan has been suspended for a long time. The only foreign coal available to Shanghai shippers and factories is Kailuan, and the only domestic coal is Boshan. If the Jiaoji Railway's mined coal is subject to a strike due to increased fees, the coal prices in the southern provinces will skyrocket, and industries will halt, which is not desired. Furthermore, the Ministry of Railways' reply to the Ministry of Industry stated that the Jiaoji and PingSui railways had special circumstances for coal transportation and that the Ministry would separately determine a reduced freight rate. The Qingji Railway Bureau cited the Xia Li reduced freight rate method, which was limited to the end of October and was therefore a separate case, not included in the Ministry of Railways' so-called reduction. This document was discussed but not implemented, greatly disappointing the coal merchants. Especially at this time of national crisis, when the people are refusing to use Japanese coal, the government should provide protection. Matters of state should be handled both according to principle and expediency, and legal matters can be amended. How can a case decided by the State Council not be subject to change? In the interest of national revenue and social stability, we are urgently telegramming Shandong mine owners to cancel the strike and urging you to order the Jiaoji Railway Bureau to temporarily retain the proposed price increase of November 1st. After the end of the war of resistance, you should convene railway bureaus and mine owners for a detailed meeting to ensure that national coal freight rates are equal and that the railway bureau's income is not reduced, the mine owners' burden is not increased, and the coal industry's future is benefited. We boldly submit these words for your consideration. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, etc. (2) To the Boshan Mine Owners United Association: The Jiaoji Railway Bureau plans to increase prices starting tomorrow, and your association has resolved to strike as a final appeal. We were extremely alarmed upon hearing this news. Shanghai's coal reserves are less than a month's worth. A halt to Shandong coal will open the door to foreign coal and block the development of domestic coal, harming social stability and the people's economy. We have jointly telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministries of Industry and Railways, and Shandong Governor Han to order the Qingji Railway to temporarily retain the price increase and for the central government to convene railway bureaus and mine owners for a detailed discussion to ensure that national revenue and mine owners' burdens are both considered and balanced. In addition to sending separate telegrams, we urge you not to strike before receiving the government's final order to avoid a coal shortage. This is our sincere request. Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, etc.

Meetings of Various Groups. During this Northeast Incident, Shanghai coal merchants unanimously resolved to stop handling Japanese coal and to stabilize coal prices. Although there have been many boycotts of Japanese goods, Japanese coal has never been included. This is truly the first righteous act. Unexpectedly, at this time of promoting domestic coal, the Jiaoji Railway suddenly increased freight rates. Shandong is a coal-producing region, and it is a major source of coal for Shanghai. Now, the Jiaoji Railway, disregarding business principles, arbitrarily increases prices, not only undermining the promotion of domestic coal and harming the Chinese people, but also affecting the work of Shanghai factories and hindering the boycott of Japanese goods. The Shandong Zichuan Weifang Mining and Coal Industry United Association specially sent representatives Li Mianmo and Yang Suwu to request assistance from all sectors of Shanghai. The night before, the Chairman of the City Chamber of Commerce, Wang Xiaolai, invited Shanghai industrial figures Xie Hengchuang, Shi Liangcai, Yu Qiaqing, Nie Lusheng, Wang Yansong, Yuan Lvdeng, Hong Yanzu, Guo Waifeng, and others to discuss rescue measures at a Yizhi Lou restaurant. A unanimous decision was reached to have the industrial and shipping groups telegram the government to fight for their rights. The summary of Li and Yang's remarks is excerpted below: Respectfully, we have learned that since the Jiaoji Railway increased coal freight rates by 20% last year, more than 100,000 tons of foreign coal has been dumped into Shandong Province. (Shandong Province was originally a coal-producing region and had no foreign coal imports. This phenomenon only occurred after the freight increase.) Exports to various ports in South China have also sharply decreased. Shandong coal merchants, seeing this dangerous situation, have repeatedly appealed for freight reductions to achieve equal treatment with other railways, but have not been granted. In May of this year, the railway suddenly announced another 20% increase. Coal merchants, already severely squeezed by the high prices, found it impossible to bear another increase and were forced to shut down. Fortunately, the government did not approve of this action, and the Jiaoji Railway voluntarily canceled the increase. Unexpectedly, on the 3rd of this month, the railway issued another notice that it would resume the 20% increase on November 1st. Upon hearing this, we were greatly alarmed. The only reason the Jiaoji Railway cited for the price increase was that, with the current boycott of Japanese coal, there would inevitably be a shortage of domestic coal, making the price increase harmless. However, at this time of national crisis, Shanghai coal merchants have discussed and unanimously boycotted Japanese coal and do not raise prices to maintain the economic stability of society. Therefore, how can the Jiaoji Railway's freight increase be said to be harmless? Merchants still know how to love their country and have this proposition. The Jiaoji Railway, as a state-run enterprise, is taking advantage of the national crisis for profit, deliberately obliterating all facts and interests and acting arbitrarily. We do not know what their intentions are. Moreover, the current coal shortage is temporary, while the price increase will be permanent, and it cannot be justified. The reason is very clear. Therefore, Shandong coal merchants are extremely indignant about the Jiaoji Railway's actions. In the past, the Jiaoji Railway's freight increase was managed by the Traffic Department. The head of the railway's Traffic Department was originally Japanese.

He aimed to prevent Shandong coal from being transported to South China, to cause a coal shortage in Shanghai, and to prevent us from insisting on the boycott, to maintain the sales market of Japanese coal in Shanghai. The plan was extremely vicious. However, according to the railway's organizational law, if the Chinese Deputy Director did not agree, his proposal could be rejected. But Deputy Director Tan was servile to the Japanese and disregarded the national crisis and commercial reports, rashly assisting in his plan. Tracing the source of the disaster, Deputy Director Tan cannot shirk his responsibility. The mine owners believe that if the Jiaoji Railway does not cancel the price increase, Shandong coal merchants will inevitably be forced to cease operations. To avoid further losses, they will have to temporarily suspend operations. However, for Shanghai, the sources of coal are Japan, Qinhuangdao, Qingdao, Tanggu, and other places. Now that Japanese coal is being boycotted, the sources have become insufficient. If Shandong coal merchants suspend operations, the source from Qingdao will be cut off, and a coal shortage in Shanghai can be predicted. The only solution is to have the Jiaoji Railway withdraw the price increase, so that merchants can be at peace. But no matter how much we explain, the railway stubbornly adheres to its decision. Therefore, our association has sent representatives south to present the situation to the government and related parties, requesting assistance to have the Jiaoji Railway cancel the price increase as soon as possible to avoid a strike and to alleviate the danger of a coal shortage in Shanghai. The Shanghai fuel problem is of great importance and has always been a concern to you all. In the past, various groups have petitioned the central government and the Shandong provincial government to cancel the price increase. Now, with the implementation of the price increase on November 10th approaching, we have not yet received a clear reply from the central government. The crisis is imminent. We urge you to discuss further assistance measures to maintain the situation. Not only will our association be eternally grateful, but the citizens of Shanghai will also benefit. October 28th, 20th year of the Republic of China,

Telegram from the Ministry of Railways. The National Coal Production and Sales Association received a telegram from the Ministry of Railways yesterday, which stated: To the Shanghai Chinese National Coal Production and Sales Association: We have received and understood your telegram regarding the soaring coal prices and the doubling of railway costs, which have made it nearly impossible to sustain operations. The Ministry has formulated relief measures and submitted them to the National Government for approval. Passenger and freight rates on all railways have been increased separately, effective May 1st of this year. The Jiaoji Railway originally planned to increase freight rates by 20%, but after repeated requests for reduction from various coal merchants, and in view of the fact that there was no issue with the price increase for domestic sales, but exports would soon be increased, and that other railways only increased by 10% or 15%, the Ministry, to show special consideration for domestic coal merchants, changed the plan and submitted it to the government for approval. The Jiaoji Railway was allowed to follow the original summer discount of 20% to offset the new price increase. It was also stated that a fair freight rate would be determined after the summer. At that time, all coal merchants expressed their compliance. During this summer discount period, the Ministry sent personnel to investigate and fully understood the high cost of coal along the railway line, which was due to (1) poor management by the mines themselves, (2) extremely high light railway freight rates, (3) Qingdao port fees, and (4) excessive shipping costs. The Jiaoji Railway's freight rate was low and could not be compared with the above factors. It could not affect coal sales. The railway bureau pointed this out to the coal merchants one by one, and the merchants had no words to defend themselves. Therefore, a compromise was reached, setting a special price of 2.8 yuan for exports, which was approximately 15% above the old price, and for domestic sales, the price was increased by 20%, as expressed by the merchants before the summer discount. This fair special price was thoroughly discussed by the Ministry and the railway before it was agreed upon. The summer discount period was also extended by one month. It can be said that the protection of domestic coal was meticulous. Currently, various coal merchants, to achieve their own selfish interests, do not hesitate to use the opportunity to exaggerate their claims and deceive the public. Some have even published articles pointing out that there are Japanese directors in various railways who are trying to undermine patriotic movements, which is completely contrary to the facts. We do not know what their intentions are. This case was initiated before May of this year. After repeated changes, a fair special price was finally determined and implemented in November, while the boycott of foreign coal only occurred after September. It can be seen that it is completely unrelated to this case. The coal merchants are only using this as a means to deceive society. Upon further review, the truth will become clear. The Ministry believes that whether domestic coal can be sold well depends primarily on whether the coal mines can produce in large quantities and secondarily on whether the railways have sufficient vehicles. Whether the freight rate is increased or not is only a matter of how much profit domestic coal can make at the current high price, and it is by no means a question of whether it can be transported to supply the market. Railway vehicles are in short supply, and military transportation is frequent, making it very difficult to allocate vehicles. Although some coal merchants with a deep understanding of righteousness plan to purchase vehicles themselves or advance funds to repair vehicles, we fear that this will be too slow to alleviate the urgent situation. If the coal merchants continue to make things difficult for the railways, it will be no different from cutting off their own business. We urge you to inform your fellow coal merchants that at this time, it is appropriate to work together to maintain the situation and seek a way out. Please do not put private interests first and disregard the overall situation. We sincerely hope so. Special reply, Ministry of Railways.

Appeal of Case Involving Death of Chinese Constable from Assault 159

Two constables on duty are accused of joint assault

Chen Taishan, from Huaian, Jiangbei, along with his uncle Chen Naiqing and his aunt Luo Chen, previously filed a lawsuit in the Second Special Court stating that their nephew Taishan was serving as Chinese constable number 632 at the Beidang Road Police Station. On the evening of September 11th of this year, after finishing his shift at 9:00 PM, he went to the Great World with four other Chinese constables, Xu Lijin (662), Hong Jiacan (607), Huang Xinchun (488), and Peng Chaoshan (493), for entertainment. They left at 11:00 PM and headed east along Avenue Edward VII. Upon reaching the entrance of Baoyu Lane, they saw a gambling stall set up by a certain Jia. Taishan went forward to gamble, leading to a quarrel with the stall owner, Jia. He was then attacked by a group of people. Xu Lijin and others helped restrain three of the assailants and handed them over to Chinese constables Yang Wende (450) and Wu Yuanyi (503) on duty at the Great Bell Police Station. Unexpectedly, Yang and Wu not only did not take the assailants to the police station but also released them and gathered twenty or thirty ruffians to attack Taishan and others, causing injury to his abdomen. He was taken to the police hospital for treatment but died on the 14th due to his injuries. Under such circumstances, the defendants Yang Wende and Wu Yuanyi are guilty of joint assault. They requested justice. After repeated summons by the court, the defendants were found not guilty. Chen Naiqing and others, dissatisfied with the first instance verdict, appealed to the Higher Third Branch Court, which was approved. Yesterday, both parties and witnesses were summoned for an investigative hearing at 2:00 PM, presided over by Criminal Division Chief Guo Dezhang, along with judges Zhang Chaozuo and Li Changnian, and prosecutor Zhang Zongkan. First, the appellant Chen Dingqing recounted the previous events and stated that his nephew was tragically killed and requested justice. Then, the four Chinese constables, Xu Lijin (662), Hong Jiacan (607), Huang Xinchun (488), and Peng Chaoshan (493), testified that on the evening of September 11th, after finishing their shift at 9:00 PM, they went to the Great World with the deceased Chen Taishan. They left after 11:00 PM and, upon reaching the entrance of Baoyu Lane, Taishan gambled at a stall, leading to a quarrel and assault with the stall owner. The civilians helped restrain three of the assailants and handed them over to constables Yang Wende (450) and Wu Yuanyi (503) on duty. Unexpectedly, the two constables released them and then gathered a crowd to attack Chen Taishan, resulting in his death. This is the truth. The official asked if the police station's report, which stated that the incident occurred because the constables demanded tips from the gambling stall, was true. Xu and others replied that it was not. The two constables, Yang Wende and Wu Yuanyi, testified that on that evening, they were on duty in that area and heard reports of a fight at the entrance of Baoyu Lane. When they arrived, patrolman number 662 said, "We are also patrolmen and can take them to the police station ourselves." There was never a case of handing over the assailants to them to take to the police station. They asked for investigation. Chief Judge Guo reviewed the testimonies and dismissed them to await further investigation at a later date.

Public Security Bureau investigation reveals those arrested were not Japanese soldiers

The local police station sent Chinese and foreign detectives to the scene, who mistakenly arrested the six students and took them to the police station. Penalties for Not Affixing Stamp Duty on Account Books and Invoices 164

Yesterday at 9:00 AM, the First District Local Court of the Special Court heard a case of violation of the Stamp Duty Regulations. Defendants Shuangwanmao Cigarette Factory in Wufulin Lane, Hongxinghao in Sanyangjing Bridge, Juchangxiang Zhenji in Shilu, Laohongyuan Shoe and Hat Store in Shujinli, China Underwear Company on Nanjing Road, Tongsanmei Wine Shop on Zhejiang Road, Hengchang Dyeing Factory in Bentang Lane Bridge North, and Yufengtai Wine Shop on Fourth Avenue were all penalized 15 yuan each by Judge Shen Shanzhen for not affixing stamp duty on invoices. Dachangxing Hardware Store at 17 Xihua Road Wuchang Road Angle was also penalized 150 yuan. Because they had been fined twice before for not complying with the stamp duty regulations and this time used disguised invoice paper with intent to evade national taxes, the penalty was increased. Dayi Hardware Store at 103 Bailaohui Road Tain Road intersection was fined 220 yuan for failing to affix stamp duty to 22 account books, after being reported by someone. The Stamp Duty Office of the Special District sent personnel and police officers with a search warrant to investigate and seize the case. Judge Shen ordered them to be fined 10 to 100 yuan per item according to the regulations. Considering that it was their first offense, the fine was reduced to 220 yuan to show a warning.

Reader's Letter

How Can We Brew a Practical and Effective Method to Boycott Japanese Goods? Liu Boyong 170

(Establish Japanese goods exhibition centers, appoint promoters, and hold oath-taking ceremonies in various places)

(1) Establish Japanese goods exhibition centers in various cities, towns, and villages. At this time, the national movement to boycott Japanese goods is heating up. There have been many inspections and seizures of Japanese goods. The general association should collect various Japanese goods and let various groups organize Japanese goods exhibition centers, planning permanent management methods. The location of the exhibition should be appropriate (in cities, such as parks or public places, such as popular temples), and the layout should be elegant. The annual sales volume of each item should be noted to allow the public to understand, so that everyone can distinguish and have feelings. Otherwise, even though people talk about boycotting Japanese goods, if you ask a passerby, "What is Japanese goods?" they will stare blankly and be unable to answer. How can they boycott it? (2) Promotion. (A) Annual promotion. After the above-mentioned Japanese goods exhibition center is established, it is necessary to hold a grand promotion ceremony, inviting all nearby residents to attend. Major promotional meetings should also be held on every national humiliation memorial day. (B) Long-term promotion. Each county should send one or two promoters to be responsible for long-term promotion of boycotting Japanese goods and promoting domestic goods. They must have the spirit of missionaries, persuading and converting people along the way. The promoters should wear hats with domestic goods trademarks and long clothes with domestic goods trademarks, holding small pamphlets with domestic goods trademarks. People with patriotic enthusiasm and willingness to serve society should be appointed, without being shy. Look at how Gandhi himself took a spinning wheel to the British palace. Domestic domestic goods factories can save their annual advertising expenses and use it as long-term promotional expenses. I am afraid it is much more effective than pasting silent slogans on wooden signs or walls. (3) Oath-taking. In major commercial ports, where anti-Japanese associations are organized, merchants should be gathered to take an oath in front of the people to never buy enemy goods. The ceremony should be very solemn and the oath should be strict.

Art World

Two Recent Female Poets in German Literary Circles 174

— Mo Jing

Among the contemporary young female poets in Germany, Ruth Schaumann and Elisabeth Motschmann can be considered to have secured a firm position in the literary world. The former gained general recognition some years ago, and now any anthology of contemporary German lyrical poetry is bound to include her work. The latter, a younger woman of twenty-three, has won the praise of such renowned German critics as Ernst Robert Curtius. Indeed, since his critique of her work, published about a year ago in the Berlin literary review, she can be considered "famous."

Ruth Schaumann is a most interesting personality. Born in Hamburg in 1899, she spent her early girlhood there, then went to Munich to study art, where she received very favorable local criticism for her sculpture. She later devoted herself to sculpture as a lifelong career. This is noteworthy because, six years ago, the critic who discussed her poetry as "sculptural lyric poetry" used many proofs to show the relationship between the two art forms to which she dedicated her life. Ruth Schaumann's first collection of poems was published in 1920, called "Die Kirche" (The Church). Reading this collection, we can say that this poet is a Catholic. Her religious and philosophical background almost uniformly permeates her work. Four years later, a dramatic poem called "Die Glashergkinder" (The Glassworks Children) appeared, along with another collection of lyrical poems called "Erde Keimende" (Germinating Earth). In 1926, another lyrical collection, "Das Buch der Hingabe" (The Book of Devotion), was published, gaining general recognition. At the same time, Ruth Schaumann also published short stories and articles on art. She has also produced works in other art forms; several of her best colored woodcuts decorate her recent collection of poems, "Was Wahr Ist" (What is True). She has also adorned "Das Buch der Hingabe" with drawings that have earned as much praise as the poems themselves.

Anyone who examines Ruth Schaumann's entire body of work can see that her work demonstrates a distinct evolution from the passionate abundance of "Erde Keimende" to the subtle seriousness of "Das Buch der Hingabe." Her book "Was Wahr Ist" is a simple display of the mystery of ordinary things—the human body seems to be merely an instrument of spiritual life, and human associations are expressed in simple, moving poems. The entire collection is a pure joy for those who have not strayed far from fundamental reality.

Elisabeth Motschmann, in any case, is not a "realist." She also insists on simple, important realities: love, health, the morning breath, and the ecstasy of spring. Some of her best poems are love poems, belonging to a kind of virginal passion. They are dedicated to the poet's beloved, and their purity and sincerity are beyond doubt. This collection also includes an excellent translation of Victor Hugo's "Booz Endormi" (Booz Asleep), whose idyllic beauty is perfectly in harmony with the poet's temperament, even when she sometimes wants to soar to a passionate rhetorical tone.

Readers of contemporary German poetry will eagerly await the publication of Elisabeth Motschmann's second collection of lyrical poems, for her first book, "Dank Des Lebens" (Thanks to Life), already foreshadows a Promise.

Death of French Sculptor Bourdelle 175

— De Ming

The modern French sculpture scene is shaped by a three-legged cauldron. Those three legs are: three great sculptors—Despiau (whose life and art the reporter introduced in an article published in the January issue of this journal), Maillol, and Bourdelle (Joseph Bourdelle). Now that we have heard of Bourdelle's death, this is not only a major loss to the French art world, but also to the art world worldwide. In mourning, I will briefly describe Bourdelle's life and art below.

Bourdelle was born in 1866 in Vienne (not Vienna, the capital of Austria; this is a county in France; readers should not misunderstand). His birthplace is located on the Rhone River, where the river winds and the mountains are intertwined, a suitable environment for nurturing the vitality of a imaginative young man. From a very young age, Bourdelle was able to carve figures of people, birds, and animals on wood. At the age of eleven, he went on to carve stone, sculpting a pair of lions and placing them in his father's garden. It can be said that his career as a sculptor began at that time. Later, he received funding from the Vienne municipal government and entered the Lyon School of Fine Arts to study sculpture. At the age of nineteen, he transferred to the National School of Fine Arts. Shortly after entering the academy, he discovered the errors in the teaching methods of the academy's teachers. Therefore, he did not follow those erroneous and outdated conventions, but took the model as his only paradigm and created faithfully. He knew that drawing was the best way to practice his skills, so he diligently practiced drawing every night, and as a result, his skills became very proficient. He did not need to make a plaster model before sculpting, but directly carved stone, with no fear of making mistakes. (Ordinary sculptors usually make a plaster model first and then carve it in stone, because they have not practiced drawing or their practice is not refined, and their skills are not smooth. Directly carving stone is feared to cause errors, so they often do not dare to try it easily.) His sculpture was simply drawing on stone, with freehand strokes that were always satisfactory. From the success of Bourdelle's art, art students can learn a very good lesson, which is that art—whether sculpture or painting—cannot succeed without focusing on drawing, because drawing is the foundation of art. Without a good and solid foundation, it is difficult to hope for artistic success.

Bourdelle's works can be divided into two main categories: reliefs and statues.

His reliefs are decorative idealist works, with a style reminiscent of ancient Greek sculpture.

His statues, however, are different from his reliefs and are naturalist works. His naturalism is thorough. In the works of any past or present sculptor, we cannot see such a thorough naturalistic style as Bourdelle's. His naturalistic works are entirely creative and do not borrow anything from others. His reliefs, as mentioned in the previous paragraph, are somewhat influenced by Greek sculpture.

Bourdelle's sculpture focuses on form (Picasso). This is different from Despiau's focus on character expression and Maillol's focus on physical expression. Character expression and physical expression have been noted by previous artists, but the issue of form has only recently begun to be noticed (such as the painting of Picasso, the leader of the modern art world, also focuses on form). Therefore, Bourdelle is an extremely ultramodern artist.

Several years ago, the French government awarded Bourdelle the Legion of Honor for his outstanding art.

Youth Corner

Withdrawal from School 176

— Ichiro

Originally studying at University B in Xujiahui, she, who was adored by many, transferred to a university in Hongkou because she disliked University B's mechanical curriculum. This news was, of course, welcomed by the male students at the Hongkou University.

She had an oval face and wore hair like black snakes. Her hobbies were eating chocolate, drinking coffee, and drinking milk. Besides eating, she liked to play tennis and basketball. As for her personality, of course, she was lively and exquisite.

Since entering the Hongkou University, she felt a sense of joy in her heart. She further developed her lively genius. Besides perfunctorily attending some classes, she played basketball and tennis on the playground.

Human personalities mostly change with the environment. She is now even more lively. Because of her lively characteristics, many male students, besides adoring her, very much wanted to pursue her.

○　○　○

One day, it was a time when autumn was swaying, she followed the school bell and stepped into the classroom.

She walked slowly forward. Unconsciously, in front of the classroom, she stepped on the foot of an athlete named Zhang. This action, in her eyes, was truly unconscious, but the manifestation of this action caused the students in the entire class to laugh and become noisy.

"She really is an unconscious woman, too romantic."

"That's for sure, I think she will be expelled by the university authorities."

"At least that's the case. You can tell from her irregular attitude."

"Besides playing ball and drinking milk, it seems that she has nothing else to do."

"She is a bored woman."

The male students in the entire class were mocking her like this. They felt an extraordinary interest in this kind of mockery. If the "meaning of life" is built on interest, then this interesting mockery is their ideal "meaning of life."

She hated their attitude very much. She thought this behavior was cruel. She became tired of school life. At the same time, she could not think of any interest in books.

She went to the principal's office crying. She said that because of special family circumstances, she requested to withdraw from school.

The principal did not object to her opinion, because he thought that children's schooling required the consent of the family.

○　○　○

She, who had been at University B for less than a month, now voluntarily withdrew from school again.

The male students at University B were repenting of their own actions.
